## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, and driven oscillators provide the structural templates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (Duffing with linear damping)
- Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * (1 + c2 * x**2) (nonlinear damping depending on amplitude)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven harmonic oscillator)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Mixed nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric + symmetric nonlinearity)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (van der Pol form with position-dependent damping)
- General polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * v**3 (general low-order nonlinear oscillator)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial in x for symmetric potentials
- Even-power terms in x (x², x⁴) break spatial symmetry — indicate asymmetric potential wells
- Velocity-position coupling terms like x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping, characteristic of self-excited oscillators (van der Pol type)
- Odd-power velocity terms (v, v³) represent dissipative forces; energy is not conserved when these are present
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates periodic external forcing — look for resonance phenomena
- If dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is conservative with a potential energy V(x) where dv_dt = -dV/dx
- Absence of explicit time dependence (no t terms) indicates an autonomous system — phase plane analysis applies
- Products of v with even powers of x (e.g., x²*v) create limit cycle behavior — energy injection at small amplitudes and dissipation at large amplitudes
- Parametric terms like x*cos(c*t) indicate parametric resonance, which differs fundamentally from direct forcing
